⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ومنعت الفلاسفة زيادته في الواجب إذ لو قام بماهيته لزم كونها قابلا وفاعلاً، وتقدمها بالوجود على الوجود ضرورة تقدم العلة على المعلول وجواز زوال الوجود عن الواجب ضرورة تقدم العلة نظراً إلى احتياجه في نفسه وأجيب عن الأول بمنع بطلان اللازم وعن الأخيرين بمنع الملازمة، إذ التقدم قد لا يكون بالوجود كالثلاثة للفردية .
·
وماهية الممكن لوجوده والمحتاج قد يمتنع زواله ضرورة كونه مقتضى الماهية) .
احتجت الفلاسفة على امتناع زيادة وجود الواجب على ماهيته بوجوده حاصلها أنه لو كان كذلك لزم محالات الأول كون الشيء قابلاً وفاعلاً وسيجيء بيان استحالته .
الثاني : تقدم الشيء بوجوده على وجوده وهو ضروري الاستحالة، لا يحتاج إلى ما ذكره الإمام من أنه يفضي إلى وجود الشيء مرتين، وإلى التسلسل في الوجودات، لأن الوجود المتقدم إن كان نفس الماهية فذاك، وإلا عاد الكلام فيه وتسلسل .
الثالث : إمكان زوال وجود الواجب وهو ضروري الاستحالة وجه اللزوم.
وأما الأول : فلأن الماهية تكون قابلاً للوجود من حيث المفروضية، وفاعلاً من حيث الاقتضاء .
وأما الثاني : فلأن الوجود يحتاج حينئذ إلى الماهية احتياج العارض إلى المعروض فيكون ممكناً ضرورة احتياجه إلى الغير فيفتقر إلى علة هي الماهية لا غير لامتناع افتقار وجود الواجب إلى الغير، وكل علة فهي متقدمة على معلولها بالضرورة، فتكون الماهية متقدمة بالوجود على الوجود.
وأما الثالث: فلأن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى غيره كان ممكناً وكان جائز الزوال نظراً إلى ذاته، وإلا لكان واجباً لذاته، هذا خلف. وإنما قلنا نظراً إلى ذاته دفعاً لما قيل : لا نسلم أن كل ممكن جائز الزوال، وإنما يكون كذلك لولم يكن واجباً بالغير ) وأجيب عن الأول : بأنا لا نسلم استحالة كون الشيء قابلاً وفاعلاً، وسيجيء الكلام على دليلها .
وعن الثاني : بأنا لا نسلم لزوم تقدم الماهية على الوجود بالوجود، وإنما يلزم ذلك لو لزم تقدم العلة على المعلول بالوجود وهو ممنوع، ودعوى الضرورة غير مسموعة ، وإنما الضرورة تقدمها بما علة به إن كانت بالوجود، فبالوجود أو بالماهية فبالماهية كما في اللوازم المستندة إلى نفس الماهية، فإن الماهية تتقدمها بذاتها ومن حيث كونها تلك الماهية من غير اعتبار وجودها أو عدمها، كالثلاثة للفردية ، وذلك كالقابل فإن تقدمه على المقبول ضروري، لكنه قد
كالأربعة للزوجية.
He said: The philosophers denied the addition of existence to the Necessary Being, for if existence were subsisting by His essence, then that essence would be both recipient and agent, and priority of the essence by existence over existence [would follow] due to the necessary priority of the cause over the effect, and the permissibility of the cessation of existence from the Necessary Being due to the necessary priority of the cause, considering its need in itself. And it was answered regarding the first by denying the invalidity of the consequent, and regarding the latter two by denying the entailment, for priority may not be by existence, like threeness for oddness. And the essence of the possible is for its existence, and the needy may be such that its cessation is impossible due to its being a necessary consequence of the essence. The philosophers argued for the impossibility of the addition of the existence of the Necessary Being to His essence by [the following] summary: if it were so, then impossibilities would follow: first, a thing being both recipient and agent, and its impossibility will be explained later. Second: priority of a thing by its existence over its existence, which is necessarily impossible, and it does not need what the Imam mentioned that it leads to a thing existing twice and to an infinite regress of existences, because if the prior existence is the essence itself, then that is it, otherwise the same argument recurs and regresses. Third: possibility of cessation of the existence of the Necessary Being, which is necessarily impossible. The manner of entailment: As for the first: because the essence would be a recipient of existence from the perspective of being supposed, and an agent from the perspective of necessitating. As for the second: because existence would then need the essence as an accident needs its substrate, so it would be possible due to its need for another, thus it would depend on a cause which is the essence alone, since it is impossible for the existence of the Necessary Being to depend on another, and every cause is necessarily prior to its effect, so the essence would be prior by existence over existence. As for the third: because if existence is in need of another, it would be possible and permissible of cessation considering itself, otherwise it would be necessary by itself, which is contrary to the assumption. And we said 'considering itself' to rebut what was said: we do not accept that every possible is permissible of cessation; rather, it is only so if it is not necessary by another. And it was answered regarding the first: we do not accept the impossibility of a thing being both recipient and agent, and the discussion of its proof will come later. Regarding the second: we do not accept the necessary priority of the essence over existence by existence; rather, that would follow only if the priority of cause over effect were by existence, and that is denied, and the claim of necessity is not admitted. Rather, the necessary priority is by that by which it is a cause: if by existence, then by existence; or by essence, then by essence—as in necessary concomitants dependent on the essence itself, for the essence is prior to them by its very self and by virtue of being that essence, without consideration of its existence or non-existence, like threeness for oddness. And that is like the recipient, for its priority over the received is necessary, but it is ... like fourness for evenness.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents a classic kalam argument: the philosophers' proof that existence is not additional to God's essence, followed by the refutation. The author begins by stating the philosophers' denial. They argue: if existence were an additional attribute subsisting in God's essence, then that essence would have to be both a recipient (qabil) of existence and an agent (fa'il) causing it—which they deem impossible. Moreover, the essence would be prior to existence by existence, since a cause must be prior to its effect, implying a vicious regress. Also, since existence depends on the essence, it would be possible for it to cease, which is impossible for the Necessary Being. The author then notes a brief preliminary answer. After this, the full argument is given as three distinct impossibilities: (1) the essence being both recipient and agent, (2) priority of a thing by its existence over its own existence, and (3) the possibility of cessation of God's existence. Each is explained in detail. Then the refutation is given: For the first, the Ash'arite position is that being both recipient and agent is not impossible—this will be argued later. For the second, the entailment of priority by existence is denied. The cause may be prior by essence, not by existence, as in the case of threeness being prior to oddness: the essence of three entails oddness without temporal priority. Thus, the essence of God can be prior to existence in terms of essence, not time. For the third, they deny that every possible is liable to cessation; a possible that is necessary by another (i.e., caused to exist perpetually) does not cease. Hence, the philosophers' proof is refuted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that priority in causality is always temporal or existential.
Correction: The Ash'arites argue that priority can be essential (bi al-dhat), as in the nature of a thing being prior to its necessary properties, without any temporal or existential sequence.

Checkpoint
How do the Ash'arites refute the philosophers' second argument about priority by existence?
A) They accept that the essence must be prior by existence but deny it leads to regress.
B) They deny that priority of cause over effect must be by existence; it can be by essence.
C) They argue that existence is eternal and does not depend on essence.
D) They claim the philosophers misunderstood the nature of existence.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'arite refutation hinges on denying that priority must be by existence and asserting that a thing can be both recipient and agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's existence and His attributes, do you unconsciously imagine a temporal sequence? What would it mean for your worship if you truly internalized that God's existence is a necessary concomitant of His essence, with no priority by existence at all?
?
The Ash'arites denied that a thing cannot be both recipient and agent. Are there areas in your life where you assume you cannot both receive from God and act for Him? How does this refutation challenge that assumption?
?
If God's essence is prior to His attributes by essence alone, not by time, then your relationship with Him is not based on a distant cause-effect chain but on a direct, essential connection. How should this affect the urgency and intimacy of your dua (supplication) today?

The First Argument: Essence as Receptive and Active
Al-Taftazani presents the first argument and its brief refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first philosophical argument that essence is prior to existence and how al-Taftazani refutes it by denying the impossibility of a thing being both receptive and active.

Core Idea
Essence is both receptive and active—but not contradictoryly.

The first argument for the priority of essence over existence claims that essence is receptive to existence when supposed and active in requiring it, implying a priority. Al-Taftazani counters by questioning the assumption that a thing cannot be both receptive and active. Let's examine the argument and its refutation closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument
Read the Arabic passage describing the first argument and its refutation. Notice how the argument sets up essence as both receptive and active.
The argument uses the terms 'قابل' (receptive) and 'فاعل' (active).
2
Understand the refutation
Al-Taftazani simply denies the impossibility of a thing being both receptive and active. Consider why this is not a full proof but a rejection of the premise.
The full proof is postponed to a later discussion.
3
Reflect on the key claim
Ask yourself: why would the philosophers think being both receptive and active is impossible? How does denying this weaken the argument?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأول : فلأن الماهية تكون قابلاً للوجود من حيث المفروضية، وفاعلاً من حيث الاقتضاء . وأما الثاني : فلأن الوجود يحتاج حينئذ إلى الماهية احتياج العارض إلى المعروض فيكون ممكناً ضرورة احتياجه إلى الغير فيفتقر إلى علة هي الماهية لا غير لامتناع افتقار وجود الواجب إلى الغير، وكل علة فهي متقدمة على معلولها بالضرورة، فتكون الماهية متقدمة بالوجود على الوجود. وأما الثالث: فلأن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى غيره كان ممكناً وكان جائز الزوال نظراً إلى ذاته، وإلا لكان واجباً لذاته، هذا خلف. وإنما قلنا نظراً إلى ذاته دفعاً لما قيل : لا نسلم أن كل ممكن جائز الزوال، وإنما يكون كذلك لولم يكن واجباً بالغير . وأجيب. عن الأول : بأنا لا نسلم استحالة كون الشيء قابلاً وفاعلاً، وسيجيء الكلام على دليلها . وعن الثاني : بأنا لا نسلم لزوم تقدم الماهية على الوجود بالوجود، وإنما يلزم ذلك لو لزم تقدم العلة على المعلول بالوجود وهو ممنوع، ودعوى الضرورة غير مسموعة ، وإنما الضرورة تقدمها بما علة به إن كانت بالوجود، فبالوجود أو بالماهية فبالماهية كما في اللوازم المستندة إلى نفس الماهية، فإن الماهية تتقدمها بذاتها ومن حيث كونها تلك الماهية من غير اعتبار وجودها أو عدمها، كالثلاثة للفردية ، وذلك كالقابل فإن تقدمه على المقبول ضروري، لكنه قد يكون بالماهية من حيث هي لا باعتبار الوجود أو العدم كماهيات الممكنات لوجوداتها . وعن الثالث : بأنا لا نسلم أن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى الماهية كان جائز الزوال عنها نظراً إلى ذاته، وإنما يلزم لو لم تكن الماهية لذاتها مقتضية له، ولا معنى لواجب الموجود سوى ما يمتنع زوال وجوده عن ذاته، نظراً إلى ذاته، ولا يضره احتياج وجوده إلى ذاته ولا تسميته ممكناً بهذا الاعتبار وإن كان خلاف الاصطلاح، فإن الممكن ما يحتاج إلى الغير في ثبوت الوجود له، فلهذا لم يتعرض في المتن للإمكان واقتصر على الاحتجاج .
As for the first: because the quiddity (al-mahiyya) is receptive to existence in terms of being supposed, and active in terms of requiring (existence). And as for the second: because existence then needs the quiddity as an accident needs its substrate, so it would be possible (mumkin) necessarily due to its need for another, thus it depends on a cause (ʿilla) which is the quiddity alone, because it is impossible for the existence of the Necessary (al-wājib) to depend on another, and every cause is prior to its effect necessarily, so the quiddity would be prior in existence to existence. And as for the third: because existence, if it needs another, would be possible and liable to annihilation in respect of itself; otherwise it would be necessary in itself, which is a contradiction. And we said 'in respect of itself' to counter the claim: we do not accept that every possible is liable to annihilation; rather it is so only if it is not necessary by another. And it was answered: Regarding the first: we do not accept the impossibility of a thing being both receptive and active, and the discussion of its proof will come later. Regarding the second: we do not accept the necessary priority of quiddity over existence in existence; that would follow only if the priority of the cause over the effect in existence were necessary, which is denied, and the claim of necessity is not admitted; rather necessity is of priority in whatever respect it is a cause: if by existence, then by existence; if by quiddity, then by quiddity, as in the concomitants (lawāzim) that are based on the quiddity itself, for the quiddity is prior to them in its essence and insofar as it is that quiddity, without consideration of its existence or non-existence, like the priority of three to oddness. And that is like the receptive (qābil): its priority to the received (maqbūl) is necessary, but it may be by the quiddity as such, not by consideration of existence or non-existence, like the quiddities of possibles to their existences. Regarding the third: we do not accept that if existence needs the quiddity it would be liable to annihilation from it in respect of itself; that would follow only if the quiddity were not, by its essence, necessitating it. And there is no meaning of 'necessary in existence' (wājib al-wujūd) except that whose existence is impossible to be removed from its essence in respect of itself, and the need of its existence for its essence does not harm it, nor does its being called possible in this respect, even if it is contrary to convention; for the possible is that which needs another for the establishment of existence for it. Hence the text (al-matn) did not address possibility and confined itself to the argument.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments from philosophers that the quiddity (essence) is prior to existence, and then refutes each. The first argument: essence is receptive to existence when supposed and active when requiring, implying priority. The answer denies the impossibility of being both. The second argument: existence needs essence like an accident needs substrate, so existence is possible and needs a cause which is essence, so essence is prior in existence. The answer distinguishes priority: the cause may be prior in a different respect (e.g., essence-priority) not necessarily existence-priority, like the priority of three to oddness. The third argument: if existence needs another, it is possible and liable to annihilation; but if essence necessitates existence, then existence cannot be removed, so it is necessary in itself, not harmed by needing its essence. Thus, possibility is about needing an external cause. The passage shows the subtlety of the relationship between essence and existence and the rejection of the philosophers' claim that essence is a cause for existence in the same way as efficient cause.

Key Terms
ماهية
قابل
فاعل
اقتضاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A thing cannot be both receptive and active in the same respect.
Correction: Al-Taftazani denies this, suggesting that being receptive and active are not contradictory.

Checkpoint
What is the core premise that al-Taftazani denies in the first argument?
A) Essence is prior to existence
B) A thing cannot be both receptive and active
C) Existence is an accident
D) Essence requires existence

Key Takeaway
The first argument for essence priority fails because its premise that a thing cannot be both receptive and active is not accepted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers assumed that a thing cannot be both receptive and active. Is there a belief you hold about yourself—that you cannot both be humble and confident, or both vulnerable and strong—that might be a false dichotomy? What would it cost you to reject that assumption today?
?
Al-Taftazani dismissed the argument by denying its premise. When you hear a claim that unsettles your worldview, do you first examine its premises, or do you instinctively reject the conclusion? How can you train yourself to think more like a mutakallim in your daily judgments?

The Second Argument: Existence Needs Essence as Accident Needs Substrate
Al-Taftazani presents the second argument and its detailed refutation focusing on the nature of causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument that existence needs essence like an accident needs its substrate, implying a causal priority, and how al-Taftazani refutes it by distinguishing priority in existence from priority in quiddity.

Core Idea
Causal priority is not always in existence; it can be in quiddity.

The second argument claims that existence depends on essence as an accident depends on its substrate, making existence contingent and requiring a cause—namely essence. Al-Taftazani refutes by denying that the cause must be prior in existence, using the example of three being prior to oddness in quiddity, not in existence. Let's explore this nuanced refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the Arabic passage for the second argument and its refutation. Note how the argument sets up existence as needing essence.
Look for the terms 'عارض' (accident) and 'معروض' (substrate).
2
Understand the refutation's key point
Al-Taftazani denies that the cause must be prior in existence. He gives an example of three and oddness. Consider why this example works.
Oddness is a concomitant of three, but three is prior by essence, not by existence.
3
Apply the principle
Think about how the quiddities of possibles are prior to their existences in a similar way, without temporal or existential priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأول : فلأن الماهية تكون قابلاً للوجود من حيث المفروضية، وفاعلاً من حيث الاقتضاء . وأما الثاني : فلأن الوجود يحتاج حينئذ إلى الماهية احتياج العارض إلى المعروض فيكون ممكناً ضرورة احتياجه إلى الغير فيفتقر إلى علة هي الماهية لا غير لامتناع افتقار وجود الواجب إلى الغير، وكل علة فهي متقدمة على معلولها بالضرورة، فتكون الماهية متقدمة بالوجود على الوجود. وأما الثالث: فلأن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى غيره كان ممكناً وكان جائز الزوال نظراً إلى ذاته، وإلا لكان واجباً لذاته، هذا خلف. وإنما قلنا نظراً إلى ذاته دفعاً لما قيل : لا نسلم أن كل ممكن جائز الزوال، وإنما يكون كذلك لولم يكن واجباً بالغير . وأجيب. عن الأول : بأنا لا نسلم استحالة كون الشيء قابلاً وفاعلاً، وسيجيء الكلام على دليلها . وعن الثاني : بأنا لا نسلم لزوم تقدم الماهية على الوجود بالوجود، وإنما يلزم ذلك لو لزم تقدم العلة على المعلول بالوجود وهو ممنوع، ودعوى الضرورة غير مسموعة ، وإنما الضرورة تقدمها بما علة به إن كانت بالوجود، فبالوجود أو بالماهية فبالماهية كما في اللوازم المستندة إلى نفس الماهية، فإن الماهية تتقدمها بذاتها ومن حيث كونها تلك الماهية من غير اعتبار وجودها أو عدمها، كالثلاثة للفردية ، وذلك كالقابل فإن تقدمه على المقبول ضروري، لكنه قد يكون بالماهية من حيث هي لا باعتبار الوجود أو العدم كماهيات الممكنات لوجوداتها . وعن الثالث : بأنا لا نسلم أن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى الماهية كان جائز الزوال عنها نظراً إلى ذاته، وإنما يلزم لو لم تكن الماهية لذاتها مقتضية له، ولا معنى لواجب الموجود سوى ما يمتنع زوال وجوده عن ذاته، نظراً إلى ذاته، ولا يضره احتياج وجوده إلى ذاته ولا تسميته ممكناً بهذا الاعتبار وإن كان خلاف الاصطلاح، فإن الممكن ما يحتاج إلى الغير في ثبوت الوجود له، فلهذا لم يتعرض في المتن للإمكان واقتصر على الاحتجاج .
As for the first: because the quiddity (al-mahiyya) is receptive to existence in terms of being supposed, and active in terms of requiring (existence). And as for the second: because existence then needs the quiddity as an accident needs its substrate, so it would be possible (mumkin) necessarily due to its need for another, thus it depends on a cause (ʿilla) which is the quiddity alone, because it is impossible for the existence of the Necessary (al-wājib) to depend on another, and every cause is prior to its effect necessarily, so the quiddity would be prior in existence to existence. And as for the third: because existence, if it needs another, would be possible and liable to annihilation in respect of itself; otherwise it would be necessary in itself, which is a contradiction. And we said 'in respect of itself' to counter the claim: we do not accept that every possible is liable to annihilation; rather it is so only if it is not necessary by another. And it was answered: Regarding the first: we do not accept the impossibility of a thing being both receptive and active, and the discussion of its proof will come later. Regarding the second: we do not accept the necessary priority of quiddity over existence in existence; that would follow only if the priority of the cause over the effect in existence were necessary, which is denied, and the claim of necessity is not admitted; rather necessity is of priority in whatever respect it is a cause: if by existence, then by existence; if by quiddity, then by quiddity, as in the concomitants (lawāzim) that are based on the quiddity itself, for the quiddity is prior to them in its essence and insofar as it is that quiddity, without consideration of its existence or non-existence, like the priority of three to oddness. And that is like the receptive (qābil): its priority to the received (maqbūl) is necessary, but it may be by the quiddity as such, not by consideration of existence or non-existence, like the quiddities of possibles to their existences. Regarding the third: we do not accept that if existence needs the quiddity it would be liable to annihilation from it in respect of itself; that would follow only if the quiddity were not, by its essence, necessitating it. And there is no meaning of 'necessary in existence' (wājib al-wujūd) except that whose existence is impossible to be removed from its essence in respect of itself, and the need of its existence for its essence does not harm it, nor does its being called possible in this respect, even if it is contrary to convention; for the possible is that which needs another for the establishment of existence for it. Hence the text (al-matn) did not address possibility and confined itself to the argument.

Commentary

The first argument: essence is receptive to existence when supposed and active when requiring, implying priority. The answer denies the impossibility of being both. The Third Argument: Existence as Contingent and Liable to Annihilation
Al-Taftazani presents the third argument and its refutation, clarifying the definition of necessary existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument that existence's need for another makes it contingent and liable to annihilation, and how al-Taftazani refutes by clarifying that if essence necessitates existence, then existence is necessary in itself, not contingently removed.

Core Idea
Existence is necessary in itself if its essence necessitates it, not liable to annihilation.

The third argument contends that existence, needing another, is possible and thus liable to annihilation unless made necessary by another. Al-Taftazani refutes by stating that if the quiddity necessitates existence, then existence cannot be removed from it in itself, so it is necessary in itself. The need for its own essence does not make it contingent. Let's unpack this subtle refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
Read the Arabic passage for the third argument and its refutation. Note how the argument uses possibility and liability to annihilation.
Look for 'جائز الزوال' (liable to annihilation).
2
Understand the refutation's core
Al-Taftazani denies that existence is liable to annihilation if its essence necessitates it. The definition of necessary existence is that existence cannot be removed in itself, even if it depends on its essence.
This is a crucial point about the nature of necessity.
3
Reflect on terminology
Note the clarification that 'possible' conventionally means needing an external cause. Here, existence's need for its own essence does not make it 'possible' in that sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأول : فلأن الماهية تكون قابلاً للوجود من حيث المفروضية، وفاعلاً من حيث الاقتضاء . وأما الثاني : فلأن الوجود يحتاج حينئذ إلى الماهية احتياج العارض إلى المعروض فيكون ممكناً ضرورة احتياجه إلى الغير فيفتقر إلى علة هي الماهية لا غير لامتناع افتقار وجود الواجب إلى الغير، وكل علة فهي متقدمة على معلولها بالضرورة، فتكون الماهية متقدمة بالوجود على الوجود. وأما الثالث: فلأن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى غيره كان ممكناً وكان جائز الزوال نظراً إلى ذاته، وإلا لكان واجباً لذاته، هذا خلف. وإنما قلنا نظراً إلى ذاته دفعاً لما قيل : لا نسلم أن كل ممكن جائز الزوال، وإنما يكون كذلك لولم يكن واجباً بالغير . وأجيب. عن الأول : بأنا لا نسلم استحالة كون الشيء قابلاً وفاعلاً، وسيجيء الكلام على دليلها . وعن الثاني : بأنا لا نسلم لزوم تقدم الماهية على الوجود بالوجود، وإنما يلزم ذلك لو لزم تقدم العلة على المعلول بالوجود وهو ممنوع، ودعوى الضرورة غير مسموعة ، وإنما الضرورة تقدمها بما علة به إن كانت بالوجود، فبالوجود أو بالماهية فبالماهية كما في اللوازم المستندة إلى نفس الماهية، فإن الماهية تتقدمها بذاتها ومن حيث كونها تلك الماهية من غير اعتبار وجودها أو عدمها، كالثلاثة للفردية ، وذلك كالقابل فإن تقدمه على المقبول ضروري، لكنه قد يكون بالماهية من حيث هي لا باعتبار الوجود أو العدم كماهيات الممكنات لوجوداتها . وعن الثالث : بأنا لا نسلم أن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى الماهية كان جائز الزوال عنها نظراً إلى ذاته، وإنما يلزم لو لم تكن الماهية لذاتها مقتضية له، ولا معنى لواجب الموجود سوى ما يمتنع زوال وجوده عن ذاته، نظراً إلى ذاته، ولا يضره احتياج وجوده إلى ذاته ولا تسميته ممكناً بهذا الاعتبار وإن كان خلاف الاصطلاح، فإن الممكن ما يحتاج إلى الغير في ثبوت الوجود له، فلهذا لم يتعرض في المتن للإمكان واقتصر على الاحتجاج .
As for the first: because the quiddity (al-mahiyya) is receptive to existence in terms of being supposed, and active in terms of requiring (existence). And as for the second: because existence then needs the quiddity as an accident needs its substrate, so it would be possible (mumkin) necessarily due to its need for another, thus it depends on a cause (ʿilla) which is the quiddity alone, because it is impossible for the existence of the Necessary (al-wājib) to depend on another, and every cause is prior to its effect necessarily, so the quiddity would be prior in existence to existence. And as for the third: because existence, if it needs another, would be possible and liable to annihilation in respect of itself; otherwise it would be necessary in itself, which is a contradiction. And we said 'in respect of itself' to counter the claim: we do not accept that every possible is liable to annihilation; rather it is so only if it is not necessary by another. And it was answered: Regarding the first: we do not accept the impossibility of a thing being both receptive and active, and the discussion of its proof will come later. Regarding the second: we do not accept the necessary priority of quiddity over existence in existence; that would follow only if the priority of the cause over the effect in existence were necessary, which is denied, and the claim of necessity is not admitted; rather necessity is of priority in whatever respect it is a cause: if by existence, then by existence; if by quiddity, then by quiddity, as in the concomitants (lawāzim) that are based on the quiddity itself, for the quiddity is prior to them in its essence and insofar as it is that quiddity, without consideration of its existence or non-existence, like the priority of three to oddness. And that is like the receptive (qābil): its priority to the received (maqbūl) is necessary, but it may be by the quiddity as such, not by consideration of existence or non-existence, like the quiddities of possibles to their existences. Regarding the third: we do not accept that if existence needs the quiddity it would be liable to annihilation from it in respect of itself; that would follow only if the quiddity were not, by its essence, necessitating it. And there is no meaning of 'necessary in existence' (wājib al-wujūd) except that whose existence is impossible to be removed from its essence in respect of itself, and the need of its existence for its essence does not harm it, nor does its being called possible in this respect, even if it is contrary to convention; for the possible is that which needs another for the establishment of existence for it. Hence the text (al-matn) did not address possibility and confined itself to the argument.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments from philosophers that the quiddity (essence) is prior to existence, and then refutes each. The first argument: essence is receptive to existence when supposed and active when requiring, implying priority. The answer denies the impossibility of being both. The second argument: existence needs essence like an accident needs substrate, so existence is possible and needs a cause which is essence, so essence is prior in existence. The answer distinguishes priority: the cause may be prior in a different respect (e.g., essence-priority) not necessarily existence-priority, like the priority of three to oddness. The third argument: if existence needs another, it is possible and liable to annihilation; but if essence necessitates existence, then existence cannot be removed, so it is necessary in itself, not harmed by needing its essence. Thus, possibility is about needing an external cause. The passage shows the subtlety of the relationship between essence and existence and the rejection of the philosophers' claim that essence is a cause for existence in the same way as efficient cause.

Key Terms
ممكن
واجب الوجود
جائز الزوال
اقتضاء
ذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If existence depends on anything (even its own essence), it must be contingent and liable to annihilation.
Correction: Dependence on one's own essence does not entail contingency; necessity is defined by the impossibility of removal in itself, regardless of essence-dependence.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, what is the condition for existence to be necessary in itself?
A) It must not need anything at all
B) Its existence cannot be removed from its essence in itself
C) It must have no cause
D) Its essence must exist prior to it

Key Takeaway
The third argument fails because existence's need for its own essence does not make it contingent—if the essence necessitates existence, existence is necessary in itself.

?
Do you ever treat God as if His existence is contingent—as if He might fail you or change? How does the truth that His existence is necessary in itself challenge that fear? Will you confess that doubt to Him today and ask for deeper trust?

The Objection of Priority and Its Refutation
Al-Taftazani refutes the claim that the giver of existence must exist before giving existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of the claim that the giver of existence must temporally precede existence, and the definition of 'giving' as the essence's requirement of existence.

Core Idea
Priority does not imply temporality; giving existence means the essence requires it.

The objector argues that the giver must exist before giving existence, similar to a craftsman. Al-Taftazani refutes this by redefining 'giving' as the essence's requirement of existence, eliminating the need for temporal priority. This lesson examines this objection and its answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objector's claim that the giver of existence must exist before giving, because the intellect cannot conceive giving without existence.
Note the comparison with the receiver who must be perceived as devoid.
2
Understand the refutation
Al-Taftazani denies the premise, stating that 'giving' here means the essence's requirement of existence, not a temporal bestowal.
Key term: iqtiḍā (requirement).
3
Follow the counter-objection
The objector then argues that if priority is not necessary, existence would be possible.
This forces a clarification about necessity.
4
See the final answer
Al-Taftazani responds that existence is necessary by itself, defined as being required by the essence.
Thus, it is not possible but necessary.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this argument guards against misunderstanding divine necessity as temporally caused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : فإن قيل : تقدم المفيد للوجود بالوجود ضروري، إذ العقل ما لم يلحظ للشيء وجود لم يمكنه تعقل كونه مفيداً لوجود بخلاف المستفيد فإنه لا بد أن يلحظ خالياً عن الوجود. قلنا : ممنوع إذ لا معنى للإفادة ههنا إلا اقتضاء الوجود لذاته، وعدم تقدمه بالوجود ضروري فإن قيل : - فيكون وجوده مطولاً فيمكن . قلنا لذاته فيجب إذ لا معنى لوجوب الوجود سوی کونه مقتضی الذات.
He said: If it is said: The priority of the giver (al-mufīd) of existence over existence is necessary, for the intellect, as long as it does not perceive existence for a thing, cannot conceive it as giving existence, unlike the receiver (al-mustafīd), for it must be perceived as devoid of existence. We say: It is denied, for there is no meaning of giving (al-ifāda) here except the requirement (iqtiḍāʾ) of existence for its essence, and its non-priority in existence is necessary. Then if it is said: Then its existence would be [؟] and thus possible. We say: (It is) necessary in itself, so it is necessary (wājib), for there is no meaning of the necessity of existence except that it is required by the essence.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This is a separate objection and answer. The objector claims that the giver of existence must exist before giving it, because the intellect cannot conceive giving existence without having existence. The answer denies this, stating that 'giving' here means merely the essence's requirement of existence, not a temporal bestowal. Thus, priority in existence is not necessary. If it is said that then existence would be possible (because it is not prior), the answer distinguishes: if existence is necessary by essence, then it is necessary, not possible. The key is that the necessity of existence is defined as being required by the essence, not by temporal priority. This guards against misunderstanding that God's existence requires a prior cause.

Correction: Priority here can mean essential priority, i.e., the essence requires existence, not that existence occurs after a prior cause.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The necessity of existence is defined by the essence's requirement, not by temporal priority.

The Philosophers' Main Argument and Its Refutation by al-Razi and al-Tusi
Al-Taftazani identifies the main philosophical argument and discusses its refutation by al-Razi and al-Tusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core argument of the philosophers regarding the cause of existence and how al-Razi and al-Tusi refuted it.

Core Idea
The philosophers' main argument is refuted by showing that the cause of existence must itself exist.

Al-Taftazani presents the central argument of the philosophers (the second aspect) and summarizes Imam al-Razi's objection. Al-Razi questions why the cause of existence could not be the quiddity itself, prior not by existence. He illustrates with examples from essentials and concomitants. Then al-Tusi refutes this by appealing to reason's judgment that a cause for an existing thing must itself exist. This lesson walks through this debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' main argument
Read the first line: 'Al-ʿumda fī iḥtijāj al-falāsifa huwa al-wajh al-thānī'. Recognize that this is the second of three arguments mentioned earlier.
The philosophers' main argument (al-ʿumda) is the second aspect.
2
Understand al-Razi's objection
Al-Razi asks: why not allow the cause of existence to be the quiddity itself, so that its priority is not by existence? Consider how this challenges the philosophers' assumption that the cause must exist prior.
3
Examine al-Razi's three analogies
Al-Razi gives three examples: (1) essentials of a quiddity are prior but not by existence, (2) quiddity is cause of its concomitants by essence not existence, (3) quiddity of the possible is receptive to existence, and priority of the receptive is necessary. Notice how each supports the idea of priority without existence.
These analogies are key to understanding his position.
4
Understand al-Tusi's refutation
Al-Tusi refutes in various places: when something is a cause for an existing thing in the external, reason (badīhat al-ʿaql) judges that the cause must have existence itself. This undermines al-Razi's proposal.
The passage ends abruptly, but the point is clear.
5
Reflect on the theological stakes
Think about why this debate matters: it concerns whether the cause of the world's existence must itself be necessary existence (Allah) or could be a quiddity. The refutation supports the necessity of a self-existent cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العمدة في احتجاج الفلاسفة هو الوجه الثاني، وحاصل ما ذكره الإمام في الجواب أنه لم لا يجوز أن يكون علة الوجود هي الماهية من حيث هي هي فتقدمه لا بالوجود كما أن ذاتيات الماهية متقدمة عليها لا بالوجود، وكما أن الماهية علة للوازمها بذاتها لا بوجودها، وكما أن ماهية الممكن قابلة لوجوده مع أن تقدم القابل أيضاً ضروري . ورده الحكيم المحقق في مواضع من الكلام فيما يكون علة لوجود أمر موجود في الخارج وبديهة العقل حاكمة
The mainstay (al-ʿumda) in the argument of the philosophers is the second aspect, and the summary of what the Imām (al-Rāzī) mentioned in the answer is: Why is it not permissible that the cause of existence be the quiddity as it is, so its priority is not by existence, just as the essentials (dhātiyyāt) of the quiddity are prior to it not by existence, and just as the quiddity is a cause for its concomitants by its essence not by its existence, and just as the quiddity of the possible is receptive to its existence while the priority of the receptive is also necessary. And the wise investigator (al-ḥakīm al-muḥaqqiq, i.e., al-Ṭūsī) refuted him in various places of his discourse concerning what is a cause for the existence of something existing in the external, and the intuition of reason judges...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage identifies the main argument of the philosophers (the second of the three mentioned earlier) and summarizes Imam al-Razi's response: why not accept that the cause of existence is the quiddity itself, and thus priority is not by existence? Examples are given: the essentials of a quiddity are prior but not by existence, the quiddity is a cause for its concomitants without existence priority, and the quiddity of the possible is receptive to its existence. Then the refutation by al-Tusi is mentioned briefly: he rejects this in several places by noting that when something is a cause for an existing thing in the external, reason judges that the cause must have existence itself. This shows the ongoing debate between theologians and philosophers.

Misconception: That the refutation of the philosophers is based on denying causality altogether.
Correction: The refutation is not about denying causality but about the nature of the cause – it must exist, not just be a quiddity.

Essence Necessitating Existence: Response to the Third Objection
Response to third objection clarifying essence-existence necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between essence and existence for the Necessary Being and why its existence is not contingent despite depending on essence.

Core Idea
The Necessary Being's existence is self-necessitated by its essence.

In this passage, the author addresses a key objection: if existence depends on essence, could it be removed? He clarifies that for the Necessary Being, essence itself necessitates existence, making removal impossible. This distinction preserves the uniqueness of the Necessary Being as self-subsistent and not dependent on an external cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to get the gist. Notice the author's concise argumentative style.
Pay attention to the opening phrase 'يكون بالماهية' which sets the context.
2
Identify the definition of wajib al-mawjud
Find the sentence where the author defines the Necessary Being. Underline the key phrase: 'ما يمتنع زوال وجوده عن ذاته'.
This definition is crucial for the whole argument.
3
Contrast with the definition of mumkin
The author gives the definition of possible being as one that needs an external cause for existence. Compare this to the Necessary Being's self-necessitation.
This distinction resolves the objection.
4
Understand the argument against the objection
The objection assumed that needing essence means contingency. The author counters by saying removal would only follow if essence did not necessitate existence. Since it does necessitate, removal is impossible.
This is the core logical move.
5
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this response is important for tawhid—it preserves God's necessary existence without making Him dependent on anything else.
The passage ends by noting the original text omitted discussion of possibility for brevity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون بالماهية من حيث هي لا باعتبار الوجود أو العدم كماهيات الممكنات لوجوداتها . وعن الثالث : بأنا لا نسلم أن الوجود إذا كان محتاجاً إلى الماهية كان جائز الزوال عنها نظراً إلى ذاته، وإنما يلزم لو لم تكن الماهية لذاتها مقتضية له، ولا معنى لواجب الموجود سوى ما يمتنع زوال وجوده عن ذاته، نظراً إلى ذاته، ولا يضره احتياج وجوده إلى ذاته ولا تسميته ممكناً بهذا الاعتبار وإن كان خلاف الاصطلاح، فإن الممكن ما يحتاج إلى الغير في ثبوت الوجود له، فلهذا لم يتعرض في المتن للإمكان واقتصر على الاحتجاج .
It is by the essence (mahiyya) in itself, not by considering existence or non-existence, like the essences of possibles for their existences. And regarding the third [objection]: we do not concede that existence, if it is in need of the essence, would be susceptible to removal from it in view of its essence. Rather, it would only be necessary if the essence in itself were not a necessitator for it. And there is no meaning for 'the necessarily existent' (wajib al-mawjud) other than that which is impossible for its existence to be removed from its essence, in view of its essence. And it does not harm it that its existence is in need of its essence, nor that it be called possible in this regard, even if it is contrary to terminology. For the possible (mumkin) is that which needs something else for the establishment of existence for it. Therefore, the text did not address possibility and confined itself to the argument.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a response to a third objection. It begins by stating that the relationship between essence and existence for the Necessary Being is by the essence itself, not by considering existence or non-existence, analogous to how the essences of possibles relate to their existences. The author then rejects the objection's implication: if existence depends on essence, it might seem removable from essence. He argues that removal would only follow if the essence did not necessitate existence. The definition of the Necessary Being is precisely that whose existence cannot be removed from its essence. Thus, the dependence of existence on essence does not make it possible (mumkin), because possibility entails need for an external cause, whereas here the necessity is self-contained. Therefore, the original text did not discuss possibility and focused on the proof.

Key Terms
ماهية (mahiyya)
وجود (wujud)
واجب الموجود (wajib al-mawjud)
ممكن (mumkin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if existence depends on essence, then the being is contingent and its existence could be removed.
Correction: The author clarifies that for the Necessary Being, its essence necessitates existence, so removal is impossible. Need does not imply contingency; only need for an external cause does.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of 'wajib al-mawjud' according to the passage?
A) That which is possible in itself
B) That which cannot have its existence removed from its essence
C) That which depends on another for existence
D) That which has no essence

Key Takeaway
The Necessary Being is defined as that whose existence is impossible to remove from its essence, thus its need for essence is self-necessitation, not contingency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that God's existence is absolutely necessary from His own essence. How does this truth challenge any area of your life where you act as if God's existence or help is optional or contingent on something else? What is one specific way you will realign your trust today?
?
The objection implies that if existence depends on essence, it could be removed. In your spiritual life, do you sometimes feel that God's presence or mercy might be removed from you? How does the knowledge that God's necessity is self-contained change how you approach Him in moments of doubt? Commit to reminding yourself of this truth when you feel distant from Him.
?
The lesson distinguishes between self-necessitation and external contingency. Are you living as if your own existence and worth are self-necessitated, or do you recognize that you are fully contingent upon the Self-Necessary One? What would it mean for your humility and reliance on God to fully accept your contingency?

The Priority of the Giver of Existence
Objection and answer about priority of giver of existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the giver of existence does not need to be prior in existence according to the author.

Core Idea
Giving existence can mean essence self-necessitation, not prior existence.

The passage begins with an objection that seems intuitive: how can something give existence without itself already being existent? The author's answer sharpens the meaning of 'giving' and shows why the objection misses the mark. This lesson walks through the objection and its precise response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and translation for the initial objection and the author's response. Notice how the objection assumes priority in existence is necessary.
The objection is based on a logical intuition about causality.
2
Understand the key redefinition
The author redefines 'giving' (ifada) not as conferring existence from a prior existent, but as the essence necessitating existence. This reframes the whole discussion.
3
Follow the follow-up objection and answer
The objector persists: if existence is not prior, then existence would be caused and thus possible. The author replies that necessity means existence is necessitated by essence, so it is not caused.
This clarifies that necessity of existence is not a property separate from essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قال) : فإن قيل : تقدم المفيد للوجود بالوجود ضروري، إذ العقل ما لم يلحظ للشيء وجود لم يمكنه تعقل كونه مفيداً لوجود بخلاف المستفيد فإنه لا بد أن يلحظ خالياً عن الوجود. قلنا : ممنوع إذ لا معنى للإفادة ههنا إلا اقتضاء الوجود لذاته، وعدم تقدمه بالوجود ضروري فإن قيل : - فيكون وجوده مطولاً فيمكن . قلنا لذاته فيجب إذ لا معنى لوجوب (الوجود سوی کونه مقتضی الذات) (1) . العمدة في احتجاج الفلاسفة هو الوجه الثاني، وحاصل ما ذكره الإمام في الجواب أنه لم لا يجوز أن يكون علة الوجود هي الماهية من حيث هي هي فتقدمه لا بالوجود كما أن ذاتيات (۲) الماهية متقدمة عليها لا بالوجود، وكما أن الماهية علة للوازمها بذاتها لا بوجودها، وكما أن ماهية الممكن قابلة لوجوده مع أن تقدم القابل أيضاً ضروري (۳) ورده الحكيم المحقق (4) في مواضع من الكلام فيما يكون علة لوجود أمر موجود في الخارج وبديهة العقل حاكمة بوجوب تقدمها عليه بالوجود فإنه ما لم يلحظ كون الشيء موجوداً امتنع أن يلحظ كونه مبدأ للوجود ومقيداً له بخلاف القابل للوجود فإنه لا بد أن باحظه العقل خالياً عن الوجود أي غير معتبر فيه الوجود لئلا يلزم حصول الحاصل، بل عن العدم أيضاً لئلا يلزم اجتماع المتنافيين. فإذن هي الماهية من حيث هي هي، وأما الذاتيات بالنسبة إلى الماهية والماهية بالنسبة إلى لوازمها فلا يجب تقدمها إلا بالوجود العقلي، لأن تقدمها بالذاتيات واتصافها بلوازمها إنما هو بحسب العقل، وإذا تحققت فتقدم قابل الوجود أيضاً كذلك لما سيجيء من أنه بحسب العقل فقط، لا كالجسم مع البياض.
(He said): If it is said: The priority of the giver of existence in existence is necessary, for the intellect does not, unless it observes existence for a thing, conceive it as a giver of existence, unlike the receiver, which must be observed devoid of existence. We say: It is denied, for there is no meaning of 'giving' here except the essence's necessitating existence, and its non-priority in existence is necessary. If it is said: Then its existence would be caused and thus possible. We say: [It is] for its essence, thus it is necessary, for there is no meaning of necessity of existence except that it is necessitated by the essence. The mainstay in the philosophers' proof is the second aspect, and the summary of what al-Imam [al-Razi] mentioned in the answer is: Why may it not be that the cause of existence is the essence in itself, so its priority is not in existence, just as the essential properties of the essence are prior to it not in existence, and just as the essence is a cause for its concomitants by its essence not by its existence, and just as the essence of the possible is receptive to its existence while the priority of the receiver is also necessary? And the verifying sage [al-Tusi] refuted this in parts of his speech regarding that which is a cause for the existence of a thing existing in the external, and the intuition of reason rules the necessity of its priority in existence, for unless the intellect observes a thing as existent, it cannot observe it as a principle of existence and a giver [of it], unlike the receiver of existence, for the intellect must observe it devoid of existence, i.e., not considering existence in it to avoid the occurrence of the already existing, rather also devoid of non-existence to avoid the conjunction of contradictories. Thus, it is the essence in itself. As for the essential properties relative to the essence, and the essence relative to its concomitants, their priority is only by intellectual existence, because their priority in essential properties and their description by concomitants is only in the mind. And if you realize this, then the priority of the receiver of existence is also similar, as will come that it is only in the mind, not like the body with whiteness.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a discussion of the philosophers' second proof. The objection states that the giver of existence must be prior in existence, because the intellect must first perceive something as existent to conceive it as a giver. The answer denies this: 'giving' here means the essence's self-necessitation, so no prior existence is needed. Then if the objector persists that this would make existence caused and thus possible, the answer is that necessity of existence means precisely that existence is necessitated by essence. Next, the author presents the core of the philosophers' second proof and summarizes al-Razi's response: the cause of existence could be the essence itself, with priority not in existence, analogous to essential properties, the essence's relation to its concomitants, and the possible's receptivity to existence. Al-Tusi refutes this, arguing that when dealing with external existence, reason demands that the cause be prior in existence, because one cannot conceive something as a principle of existence without it being existent. He distinguishes this from the case of a receiver, which must be conceived devoid of both existence and non-existence to avoid the occurrence of the already existing or the conjunction of contradictories. The passage concludes by clarifying that the priority in such cases is only in the mind (wujud 'aqli), not in external reality.

Key Terms
مفيد للوجود (mufid li'l-wujud)
قابل (qabil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The giver of existence must be prior in existence because he must exist before giving.
Correction: The author clarifies that 'giving' here means the essence necessitating existence, not a temporal transfer, so no prior existence is required.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the giver of existence does not need priority in existence?
A) Because giving existence is metaphorical
B) Because the essence necessitates existence without prior existence
C) Because the giver is not existent
D) Because priority is impossible

Key Takeaway
The giver of existence does not require priority in existence when 'giving' means self-necessitation of existence by the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you ever think of it as given by a Giver? Does this lesson challenge you to see God's existence as necessitated by His essence, not as something that came from elsewhere? How does that change your sense of reliance on Him?
?
If God's existence is not prior to His giving existence, then He is not a 'giver' in the way we give gifts. Have you ever thought of God as 'giving' existence like a donation? How must you adjust your understanding of His absolute self-sufficiency?
?
This argument protects God from being considered 'possible' or 'caused'. Have you ever had even a subtle thought that God might owe His existence to something else? What is at stake for your faith if that thought enters your heart?

Philosophers' Second Proof: Al-Razi vs Al-Tusi
Debate on the second proof: al-Razi's response and al-Tusi's refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' second proof and the critical debate between al-Razi and al-Tusi about the priority of the cause.

Core Idea
The cause of external existence must be prior in existence; mental priority is different.

After the initial exchange, the author presents the mainstay of the philosophers' proof and summarizes al-Razi's creative response, which draws analogies from essential properties and mental existence. Al-Tusi's refutation then clarifies a crucial distinction: when dealing with real external existence, the cause must be observed as existent first. This lesson unpacks that debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second proof
Read the passage starting from 'al-umda fi ihtijaj al-falasifa' to understand the core of the philosophers' argument.
This proof is the main one according to the author.
2
Understand al-Razi's analogies
Al-Razi proposes that the cause of existence could be the essence itself, not requiring priority in existence, analogous to essential properties, essence as cause of concomitants, and the possible's receptivity.
These analogies rely on mental existence.
3
Grasp al-Tusi's refutation
Al-Tusi argues that for external existence, the cause must be prior in existence; otherwise the intellect cannot conceive it as a principle of existence.
He distinguishes between receiver (must be devoid) and giver (must be existent).
4
Distinguish mental vs external priority
The passage concludes that priority in essential properties and receptivity is only in the mind (wujud 'aqli), not in external reality.
This resolves the debate by clarifying the domain.

Source Text

(He said): If it is said: The priority of the giver of existence in existence is necessary, for the intellect does not, unless it observes existence for a thing, conceive it as a giver of existence, unlike the receiver, which must be observed devoid of existence. The objection states that the giver of existence must be prior in existence, because the intellect must first perceive something as existent to conceive it as a giver. Misconception: The cause of existence always has priority in existence, even in mental existence.
Correction: Al-Tusi distinguishes: for external existence, the cause must be prior in existence; but for mental existence, priority can be non-existential, as in essential properties.

Self-Necessitation Defines Necessity, Not Contingency
The author presents his own verification and answers the final objection that essence-causation implies contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument that essence-causation implies contingency fails, and how self-necessitation defines necessity, not possibility.

Core Idea
Self-necessitation is the very meaning of necessity, not a cause of contingency.

In this passage, the author addresses a subtle objection: if Allah's essence gives existence to itself, does that not make His existence an effect and therefore contingent? The author explains that this misunderstanding arises from confusing two different types of causation. By carefully analyzing the terms, he shows that self-necessitation actually defines necessity, not possibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the objection that essence-causation implies possibility, and the author's response that self-necessitation defines necessity.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the distinction between giving existence to oneself vs. to another
The author first clarifies that self-giving does not require priority because the essence necessitates existence instantaneously, unlike giving existence to another which requires pre-existence.
This sets up the refutation.
3
See how the author refutes the claim that self-necessitation implies possibility
The objection argues that if essence causes existence, then existence is an effect, and all effects are possible. The author counters that the 'effect' here is existence itself, and the 'cause' is the essence, so the relation defines necessity, not possibility.
Focus on the phrase 'لا نسلم أن كل معلول للغير بهذا المعنى ممكن'.
4
Reflect on the final analysis of necessity of existence
The author concludes that describing existence as necessary means it is necessitated by the essence without any external need. This is the core of his verification.
Contrast with the earlier misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنقول على طريق البحث دون التحقيق : لا نسلم أن المفيد لوجود نفسه يلزم تقدمه عليه بالوجود، فإنه لا معنى للإفادة سوی أن تلك الماهية تقتضي لذاتها الوجود ويمتنع تقدمها عليه بالوجود ضرورة امتناع حصول الحاصل كما في القابل بعينه بخلاف المقيد لوجود الغير، فإن بديهة العقل حاكمة بأنه ما لم يكن موجوداً لم يكن مبدأ لوجود الغير (۱) ومن ههنا يستدل بالعالم على وجود الصانع . فإن قيل: إذا كانت ماهية الواجب مفيدة لوجوده ومقتضية له كان وجوده معلولاً للغير، وكل معلول للغير ممكن فيكون وجود الواجب ممكناً، هذا خلف (٢). قلنا بعد المساعدة على تسمية مقتضى الماهية معلولاً لها وتسمية الذات الموجودة غير الوجود لا نسلم أن كل معلول للغير بهذا المعنى ممكن، وإنما يلزم ذلك لو لم يكن المعلول هو الوجود والغير هو الماهية التي قام بها ذلك الوجود، كيف ولا معنى لوجوب الوجود سوى كونه مقتضى الذات التي قام بها الوجود من غير احتياج إلى غير تلك الذات؟ وهذا معنى قوله قلنا لذاته فيجب أن يكون وجود الواجب مقتضى لذات الواجب، فيكون اللازم وجوبه لا إمكانه وتحقيقه. إنا إذا وصفنا الماهية بالوجوب فمعناه أنها لذاتها تقتضي الوجود، وإذا وصفنا به الوجود فمعناه أنه مقتضى ذات الماهية من غير احتياج إلى غيرها .
We say, by way of investigation without verification: We do not concede that the giver of existence to itself requires its priority in existence, for there is no meaning of 'giving' except that that essence necessitates existence for itself, and its priority in existence is impossible due to the impossibility of the occurrence of the already existing, just as in the case of the receiver itself, unlike the giver of existence to another, for the intuition of reason rules that unless it is existent, it cannot be a principle of existence for another. And from this is deduced from the world the existence of the Maker. If it is said: If the essence of the Necessary is giving to its existence and necessitating it, then its existence would be an effect of another, and every effect of another is possible, so the existence of the Necessary would be possible; this is a contradiction. We say: After conceding to naming the necessitated of the essence as its effect and naming the existing essence as other than existence, we do not concede that every effect of another in this sense is possible. Rather, it would only be necessary if the effect were not existence and the other were not the essence which that existence subsists in. How so, and there is no meaning for 'necessity of existence' except that it is necessitated by the essence which existence subsists in, without need for anything other than that essence? And this is the meaning of his statement: 'We say: for its essence, thus it is necessary' – that the existence of the Necessary is necessitated by the essence of the Necessary, so the consequent is its necessity, not its possibility. Indeed, when we describe the essence by necessity, its meaning is that it necessitates existence for itself; and when we describe existence by it, its meaning is that it is necessitated by the essence, without need for anything else.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents the commentator's own verification and then addresses a final objection. The commentator first states that, methodologically speaking, one does not concede that the self-giver of existence requires priority in existence; 'giving' here means the essence necessitates existence, and priority is impossible because it would involve the occurrence of what already exists. This differs from giving existence to another, where the giver must exist. From this, one can argue from the world to the existence of the Maker. Then an objection arises: if the Necessary's essence gives existence to itself, then existence is an effect of another (the essence), and every effect of another is possible, implying the Necessary would be possible—a contradiction. The answer: even if one accepts the terms, not every effect in this sense is possible. The effect here is existence, and the other is the essence itself, so the relationship defines necessity, not possibility. Necessity of existence means precisely that existence is necessitated by the essence without need for anything else. Thus, describing the essence as necessary means it necessitates existence for itself, and describing existence as necessary means it is necessitated by the essence.

Key Terms
مقتضي الذات (muqtada al-dhat)
معلول (ma'lul)
وجوب الوجود (wujub al-wujud)
إمكان (imkan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah's essence gives existence to itself, then His existence is an effect and therefore contingent.
Correction: Self-necessitation is precisely what necessity means; it does not imply contingency because the 'cause' is the essence itself, not an external factor.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'necessity of existence' mean?
A) Existence is caused by an external cause
B) Existence is necessitated by the essence without need for anything else
C) Existence is impossible
D) Existence is accidental

Key Takeaway
Self-necessitation is the essence of necessity, not a cause of contingency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's essence necessitates His existence without any need, what does that say about your own existence? Are you necessary or contingent? How does your contingency shape your daily reliance on Him?
?
The author says 'there is no meaning for necessity of existence except that it is necessitated by the essence.' How does knowing that God's very essence makes Him necessary affect your worship and trust in Him? In what areas of your life do you still act as if God is not necessary?
?
If the Necessary Being has no cause for His existence, then He alone is self-sufficient. Where in your life are you still seeking sufficiency from created things instead of from the One whose essence is self-sufficiency? What specific step will you take today to turn back to Him alone?

Refuting the Claim that the Mahiyya's Necessitation of Existence Implies Possibility
The author refutes the objection that essential necessitation implies possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between internal essential causation and external causal chains, and why the mahiyya's necessitation does not entail possibility.

Core Idea
Essential necessity is not the same as created causality; the mahiyya's act of giving existence is not an external cause.

In this passage, the author addresses a critical objection: if the essence of the Necessary Being gives existence to itself, doesn't that make existence an effect? And doesn't every effect point to possibility? By carefully distinguishing between internal essential necessity and external causation, the author defends the coherence of wajib al-wujud.

Guided Path
1
Read the entire passage
Read both the Arabic and the English translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice that the passage contains an objection and its refutation.
Pay attention to the flow: author's initial denial, then the objection (فإن قيل), then the response (قلنا).
2
Identify the objection
Find the sentence starting with 'فإن قيل' and understand its claim: if the essence gives existence, then existence is an effect of another, and every effect of another is possible, making the Necessary possible.
This objection would undermine the concept of wajib al-wujud.
3
Analyze the refutation
The author accepts the terminology but rejects the inference. Focus on why 'effect' here does not imply possibility. The key is that the 'other' here is the essence itself, not an external cause.
The author emphasizes that necessity of existence means the essence itself necessitates existence without any external cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنقول على طريق البحث دون التحقيق : لا نسلم أن المفيد لوجود نفسه يلزم تقدمه عليه بالوجود، فإنه لا معنى للإفادة سوی أن تلك الماهية تقتضي لذاتها الوجود ويمتنع تقدمها عليه بالوجود ضرورة امتناع حصول الحاصل كما في القابل بعينه بخلاف المقيد لوجود الغير، فإن بديهة العقل حاكمة بأنه ما لم يكن موجوداً لم يكن مبدأ لوجود الغير (۱) ومن ههنا يستدل بالعالم على وجود الصانع . هاهنا 6 فإن قيل : إذا كانت ماهية الواجب مفيدة لوجوده ومقتضية له كان وجوده معلولاً للغير، وكل معلول للغير ممكن فيكون وجود الواجب ممكناً، هذا خلف (٢). قلنا بعد المساعدة على تسمية مقتضى الماهية معلولاً لها وتسمية الذات الموجودة غير الوجود لا نسلم أن كل معلول للغير بهذا المعنى ممكن، وإنما يلزم ذلك لو لم يكن المعلول هو الوجود والغير ، هو الماهية التي قام بها ذلك الوجود، كيف ولا معنى لوجوب الوجود سوى كونه مقتضى الذات التي قام بها الوجود من غير احتياج إلى غير تلك الذات؟ وهذا معنى قوله قلنا لذاته فيجب أن يكون وجود الواجب مقتضى لذات الواجب، فيكون اللازم وجوبه لا إمكانه وتحقيقه. إنا إذا وصفنا الماهية بالوجوب فمعناه أنها لذاتها تقتضي الوجود، وإذا وصفنا به الوجود فمعناه أنه مقتضى ذات الماهية من غير احتياج إلى غيرها . فسواء قلنا واجب الوجود لذاته أو الوجود واجب لذاته فالمراد ذات الموجود لا ذات الوجود.
We say in the manner of investigation without verification: We do not accept that the one that gives existence to itself necessitates its priority over it in existence. For the meaning of 'giving' is only that that essence (mahiyya) necessitates existence by itself, and it is impossible for it to be prior to it in existence due to the impossibility of obtaining the already obtained, exactly like in the case of the receptacle, contrary to the qualifier of the existence of another. For the intuition of the intellect judges that as long as it is not existing, it is not a source of the existence of another. From this, one infers from the world the existence of the Maker. Here [there is an objection:] If the essence of the Necessary is that which gives and necessitates its existence, then its existence would be an effect of another, and every effect of another is possible, so the existence of the Necessary would be possible, which is a contradiction. We say: After accepting the naming of that which is necessitated by the essence as an effect of it, and the naming of the existing essence as other than existence, we do not accept that every effect of another in this sense is possible. That would only follow if the effect were existence and the other were the essence that subsists by that existence. How so? For the meaning of necessity of existence is only that it is necessitated by the essence that subsists by existence without need for other than that essence. This is the meaning of His saying 'by itself' (li-dhatihi). Therefore, the existence of the Necessary must be necessitated by the essence of the Necessary, so the necessary consequent is its necessity, not its possibility, and its realization. When we describe the essence as necessary, it means that it by itself necessitates existence. And when we describe existence as necessary, it means that it is necessitated by the essence without need for anything else. So whether we say 'the Necessary of existence by itself' or 'existence is necessary by itself', the referent is the existing essence, not the essence of existence.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage begins with the author's response to an earlier argument. He denies that the one that gives existence to itself requires priority of existence over essence. He explains that 'giving' means the essence itself necessitates existence, and priority is impossible to avoid circularity. Then an objection is raised: if the essence of the Necessary Being gives and necessitates its existence, then existence becomes an effect of the essence, making it possible. The author responds by first accepting the terminology but then rejecting the inference. He says that calling the essence a 'cause' and existence an 'effect' does not entail possibility, because the effect here is existence and the 'other' is the essence that exists with existence. The necessity of existence means that the essence itself necessitates existence without any external cause. Thus the conclusion is necessity, not possibility. The author clarifies that describing the essence as 'necessary by itself' means it necessitates existence by itself, and describing existence as 'necessary' means it is necessitated by the essence. Both statements ultimately refer to the same reality: the existing essence.

qabil
mahiyya
wajib al-wujud
mujib
illa
ma'lul
hujul al-hasil
badiha al-aql

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if the essence causes existence, then existence must be possible, because causation implies contingency.
Correction: The author clarifies that 'causing' here is not external causation but essential necessity, which does not entail possibility.

Checkpoint
In the objection, why would existence being an effect of the essence imply possibility?
A) Because all effects of an external cause are possible.
B) Because the essence is prior to existence in reality.
C) Because the existence of the Necessary is contingent.
D) Because the objection misinterprets 'effect' as external causation.

Key Takeaway
Essential necessity means the essence itself necessitates existence without external cause, so no possibility is entailed.

?
The objection that essential necessity implies possibility is subtle. Have you ever doubted or questioned God's necessity in your heart, even for a moment? How does this passage's response address that doubt personally? What step will you take to root out any lingering assumption that God could be otherwise?

Five Proofs for the Addition of Existence to Essence
The mutakallimun present five arguments that existence is additional to the essence of the Necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five proofs used by the mutakallimun to argue that existence is additional to the essence of the Necessary Being, and the response that these proofs only apply to specific existence.

Core Idea
Existence is not identical to essence in the Necessary; five proofs demonstrate their addition.

The mutakallimun (theologians) developed precise arguments to show that the existence of God is not simply identical to His essence but is an additional attribute. In this lesson, we examine five of their key proofs, followed by an important clarification that the dispute concerns specific existence, not absolute existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the five proofs and the answer. Note the numbered structure.
The passage lists proofs from 'first' to 'fifth'.
2
Analyze each proof individually
Go through each proof one by one. Understand the logical structure: each proof assumes existence is not part of the essence and deduces a problem.
Pay attention to the conditional reasoning in proofs 1, 2, and 4.
3
Examine the answer to the proofs
Read the response: these proofs only show addition for specific existence, not absolute existence. Understand the limitation.
The answer says the dispute is about specific existence (al-wujud al-khas), not absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq).
4
Summarize in your own words
Write a short summary of the five proofs and the answer. Test your understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدلة المتكلمين على زيادة وجود الواجب على ماهيته قال : وعورضت بوجوده الأول: لو لم يكن وجود الواجب مقارناً لماهيته فتجرده إما لذاته فيعم الكل، أو لغيره فيحتاج إلى الواجب . الثاني: مبدأ الممكنات حينئذ إما الوجود وحده فيكون الشيء مبدأ لنفسه ولعلله . وإما مع التجرد شطراً فيتركب الواجب أو شرطاً فيكون كل وجود مبدأ لكل شيء ويتخلف عنه الأثر لفقد شرطه لا لذاته . الثالث: الواجب يشارك الممكنات في الوجود ويخالفها في الحقيقة فيتغايران. الرابع: الواجب إن كان مجرد الكون تعدد أو مع التجرد تركب، أو شرطه افتقر ، وإن كان غيره فإن كان بدون الكون ،فمحال وإن كان معه فزائد ضرورة امتناع كونه داخلاً . الخامس : الوجود معلوم ضرورة بخلاف الواجب . وأجيب بأنه لا نزاع في زيادة الوجود المطلق بل الخاص وما ذكر لا يدل عليه استدل المتكلمون على زيادة وجود الواجب على ماهيته بوجوه :
The proofs of the mutakallimun for the addition of the existence of the Necessary to its essence. He said: It was objected by its existence. First: If the existence of the Necessary were not concomitant with its essence, then its abstraction [from existence] would be either by itself, in which case it would apply to everything, or by another, in which case it would need the Necessary. Second: The source of possibles would then be either existence alone, in which case a thing would be the source of itself and of its causes; or [existence] together with abstraction as a part, in which case the Necessary would be composed, or as a condition, in which case every existence would be a source of everything and the effect would be absent due to the lack of its condition, not due to itself. Third: The Necessary shares with possibles in existence and differs from them in reality, so they are two different things. Fourth: If the Necessary were merely 'being' (al-kawn), it would be multiple; or with abstraction, it would be composed; or its condition would make it in need; and if it were other than that, then if it were without 'being', it is impossible, and if with it, then it is additional due to the impossibility of its being internal. Fifth: Existence is known by necessity, unlike the Necessary. And the answer was that there is no dispute about the addition of absolute existence, but [only] of specific existence, and what was mentioned does not indicate it. The mutakallimun argued for the addition of the existence of the Necessary to its essence with proofs.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents five proofs (adilla) used by the mutakallimun (theologians) to demonstrate that existence (wujud) is additional to (za'id 'ala) the essence (mahiyya) of the Necessary Being. The proofs are: (1) If existence were not concomitant with essence, then existence would either be abstracted by itself (applying to all essences, absurd) or by another (needing the Necessary). (2) The source of possibles would be existence alone (leading to self-causation) or with abstraction (causing composition or conditionality). (3) The Necessary shares existence with possibles but differs in reality, indicating distinction. (4) If the Necessary is just 'being', it would be multiple; if with abstraction, composite; if condition, dependent; otherwise impossible. (5) Existence is known necessarily, unlike the Necessary. The answer given is that the dispute is not about absolute existence but specific existence, and these proofs do not demonstrate that. The passage ends with a repetition of the claim that the mutakallimun argue for addition with proofs.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These proofs show that existence is separate from essence in God in an absolute sense.
Correction: The answer clarifies that the proofs only establish addition for specific existence (al-wujud al-khas), not absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq), so the separation is not absolute.

Checkpoint

B) Either existence would be abstracted by itself (applying to all) or by another (needing the Necessary).
C) The Necessary would be multiple.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun provided five proofs that existence is additional to essence in the Necessary, but the answer restricts this to specific existence, not absolute existence.

The answer in the passage restricts the addition to specific existence. Have you ever confused your limited understanding of God with His true reality? How can you cultivate humility before the mystery of divine existence?
?
Consider the fifth proof: existence is known necessarily, but God is not known necessarily. How often do you affirm God's existence without truly knowing Him? What step will you take today to move from mere belief to intimate knowledge?
